<p><b>Sir Muhammad Iqbal</b> (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Urdu_language" title="Urdu language">Urdu</a>: <span dir="rtl" lang="ur" xml:lang="ur"><span class="Nastaliq" style="font-size: 125%; font-family: 'Jameel Noori Nastaleeq', 'Urdu Typesetting', 'Noto Nastaliq Urdu', 'Noto Nastaliq Urdu Draft', 'Hussaini Nastaleeq', 'AlQalam Taj Nastaleeq', IranNastaliq, 'Awami Nastaliq', 'Awami Nastaliq Beta4', 'Awami Nastaliq Beta3', 'Awami Nastaliq Beta2', 'Awami Nastaliq Beta1', 'Nafees Nastaleeq', 'Nafees Nastaleeq v1.01', 'Pak Nastaleeq', 'PDMS_Jauhar', 'Alvi Lahori Nastaleeq';" title="Nastaliq">محمد اقبال</span></span> ‎) (November 9, 1877 – April 21, 1938), widely known as <b>Allama Iqbal</b> (<span lang="ur" xml:lang="ur"><span class="Nastaliq" style="font-size: 125%; font-family: 'Jameel Noori Nastaleeq', 'Urdu Typesetting', 'Noto Nastaliq Urdu', 'Noto Nastaliq Urdu Draft', 'Hussaini Nastaleeq', 'AlQalam Taj Nastaleeq', IranNastaliq, 'Awami Nastaliq', 'Awami Nastaliq Beta4', 'Awami Nastaliq Beta3', 'Awami Nastaliq Beta2', 'Awami Nastaliq Beta1', 'Nafees Nastaleeq', 'Nafees Nastaleeq v1.01', 'Pak Nastaleeq', 'PDMS_Jauhar', 'Alvi Lahori Nastaleeq';" title="Nastaliq">علامہ اقبال</span></span>), was a poet, philosopher, and politician, as well as an academic, barrister and scholar<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aml.org.pk_2-0"><a href="#cite_note-aml.org.pk-2">[2]</a></sup> in <a href="/wiki/British_Raj" title="British Raj">British India</a> who is widely regarded as having inspired the <a href="/wiki/Pakistan_Movement" title="Pakistan Movement">Pakistan Movement</a>. He is called the "Spiritual father of Pakistan".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup> He is considered one of the most important figures in <a href="/wiki/Urdu_literature" title="Urdu literature">Urdu literature</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-goethezeitportal_4-0"><a href="#cite_note-goethezeitportal-4">[4]</a></sup> with literary work in both the <a href="/wiki/Urdu" title="Urdu">Urdu</a> and <a href="/wiki/Persian_language" title="Persian language">Persian</a> languages.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aml.org.pk_2-1"><a href="#cite_note-aml.org.pk-2">[2]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-goethezeitportal_4-1"><a href="#cite_note-goethezeitportal-4">[4]</a></sup></p>
<p>Iqbal is admired as a prominent poet by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pakistani_people" title="Pakistani people">Pakistanis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Indian_people" title="Indian people">Indians</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Iranian_people" title="Iranian people">Iranians</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bangladeshi_people" title="Bangladeshi people">Bangladeshis</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sri_Lankan_Tamil_people" title="Sri Lankan Tamil people">Sri Lankans</a> and other international scholars of literature.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-thefriday_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-thefriday-5">[5]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dailytimes.co.pk_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-dailytimes.co.pk-6">[6]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Iqbal_Academy_Pakistan_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-Iqbal_Academy_Pakistan-7">[7]</a></sup> Though Iqbal is best known as an eminent poet, he is also a highly acclaimed "Muslim philosophical thinker of modern times".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aml.org.pk_2-2"><a href="#cite_note-aml.org.pk-2">[2]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Iqbal_Academy_Pakistan_7-1"><a href="#cite_note-Iqbal_Academy_Pakistan-7">[7]</a></sup> His first poetry book, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Secrets_of_the_Self" title="The Secrets of the Self">Asrar-e-Khudi</a></i>, appeared in the Persian language in 1915, and other books of poetry include <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rumuz-i-Bekhudi" title="Rumuz-i-Bekhudi">Rumuz-i-Bekhudi</a></i>, <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Payam-i-Mashriq" title="Payam-i-Mashriq">Payam-i-Mashriq</a></i> and <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Zabur-i-Ajam" title="Zabur-i-Ajam">Zabur-i-Ajam</a></i>. Amongst these, his best known Urdu works are <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bang-i-Dara" title="Bang-i-Dara">Bang-i-Dara</a></i>, <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bal-i-Jibril" title="Bal-i-Jibril">Bal-i-Jibril</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Rod_of_Moses" title="The Rod of Moses">Zarb-i Kalim</a></i> and a part of <i><a href="/wiki/Gift_from_Hijaz" title="Gift from Hijaz">Armughan-e-Hijaz</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-allamaiqbal.com_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-allamaiqbal.com-8">[8]</a></sup> Along with his Urdu and Persian poetry, his Urdu and English lectures and letters have been very influential in cultural, social, religious and political disputes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-allamaiqbal.com_8-1"><a href="#cite_note-allamaiqbal.com-8">[8]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1922, he was <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Knighthood" title="Knighthood">knighted</a> by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/George_V_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="George V of the United Kingdom">King George V</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup> granting him the title "Sir".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-groundreport.com_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-groundreport.com-10">[10]</a></sup> While studying law and philosophy in England, Iqbal became a member of the London branch of the <a href="/wiki/All-India_Muslim_League" title="All-India Muslim League">All-India Muslim League</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Iqbal_Academy_Pakistan_7-2"><a href="#cite_note-Iqbal_Academy_Pakistan-7">[7]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-allamaiqbal.com_8-2"><a href="#cite_note-allamaiqbal.com-8">[8]</a></sup> Later, during the League's December 1930 session, he delivered his most famous presidential speech known as the <a href="/wiki/Allahabad_Address" title="Allahabad Address">Allahabad Address</a> in which he pushed for the creation of a <a href="/wiki/Pakistan" title="Pakistan">Muslim state</a> in Northwest India.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Iqbal_Academy_Pakistan_7-3"><a href="#cite_note-Iqbal_Academy_Pakistan-7">[7]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-allamaiqbal.com_8-3"><a href="#cite_note-allamaiqbal.com-8">[8]</a></sup></p>
<p>In much of South Asia and the Urdu speaking world, Iqbal is regarded as the <i>Shair-e-Mashriq</i> (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Urdu_language" title="Urdu language">Urdu</a>: <span dir="rtl" lang="ur" xml:lang="ur"><span class="Nastaliq" style="font-size: 125%; font-family: 'Jameel Noori Nastaleeq', 'Urdu Typesetting', 'Noto Nastaliq Urdu', 'Noto Nastaliq Urdu Draft', 'Hussaini Nastaleeq', 'AlQalam Taj Nastaleeq', IranNastaliq, 'Awami Nastaliq', 'Awami Nastaliq Beta4', 'Awami Nastaliq Beta3', 'Awami Nastaliq Beta2', 'Awami Nastaliq Beta1', 'Nafees Nastaleeq', 'Nafees Nastaleeq v1.01', 'Pak Nastaleeq', 'PDMS_Jauhar', 'Alvi Lahori Nastaleeq';" title="Nastaliq">شاعر مشرق</span></span>‎, "Poet of the East").<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Abida_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-Abida-11">[11]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pktoday73_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-pktoday73-12">[12]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dailytimes_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-dailytimes-13">[13]</a></sup> He is also called <i>Mufakkir-e-Pakistan</i> (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Urdu_language" title="Urdu language">Urdu</a>: <span dir="rtl" lang="ur" xml:lang="ur"><span class="Nastaliq" style="font-size: 125%; font-family: 'Jameel Noori Nastaleeq', 'Urdu Typesetting', 'Noto Nastaliq Urdu', 'Noto Nastaliq Urdu Draft', 'Hussaini Nastaleeq', 'AlQalam Taj Nastaleeq', IranNastaliq, 'Awami Nastaliq', 'Awami Nastaliq Beta4', 'Awami Nastaliq Beta3', 'Awami Nastaliq Beta2', 'Awami Nastaliq Beta1', 'Nafees Nastaleeq', 'Nafees Nastaleeq v1.01', 'Pak Nastaleeq', 'PDMS_Jauhar', 'Alvi Lahori Nastaleeq';" title="Nastaliq">مفکر پاکستان</span></span>‎, "The Thinker of Pakistan"), <i>Musawar-e-Pakistan</i> (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Urdu_language" title="Urdu language">Urdu</a>: <span dir="rtl" lang="ur" xml:lang="ur"><span class="Nastaliq" style="font-size: 125%; font-family: 'Jameel Noori Nastaleeq', 'Urdu Typesetting', 'Noto Nastaliq Urdu', 'Noto Nastaliq Urdu Draft', 'Hussaini Nastaleeq', 'AlQalam Taj Nastaleeq', IranNastaliq, 'Awami Nastaliq', 'Awami Nastaliq Beta4', 'Awami Nastaliq Beta3', 'Awami Nastaliq Beta2', 'Awami Nastaliq Beta1', 'Nafees Nastaleeq', 'Nafees Nastaleeq v1.01', 'Pak Nastaleeq', 'PDMS_Jauhar', 'Alvi Lahori Nastaleeq';" title="Nastaliq">مصور پاکستان</span></span>‎, "Artist of Pakistan") and <i>Hakeem-ul-Ummat</i> (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Urdu_language" title="Urdu language">Urdu</a>: <span dir="rtl" lang="ur" xml:lang="ur"><span class="Nastaliq" style="font-size: 125%; font-family: 'Jameel Noori Nastaleeq', 'Urdu Typesetting', 'Noto Nastaliq Urdu', 'Noto Nastaliq Urdu Draft', 'Hussaini Nastaleeq', 'AlQalam Taj Nastaleeq', IranNastaliq, 'Awami Nastaliq', 'Awami Nastaliq Beta4', 'Awami Nastaliq Beta3', 'Awami Nastaliq Beta2', 'Awami Nastaliq Beta1', 'Nafees Nastaleeq', 'Nafees Nastaleeq v1.01', 'Pak Nastaleeq', 'PDMS_Jauhar', 'Alvi Lahori Nastaleeq';" title="Nastaliq">حکیم الامت</span></span>‎, "The Sage of the <a href="/wiki/Ummah" title="Ummah">Ummah</a>"). The Pakistan government officially named him a "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_national_poets" title="List of national poets">national poet</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Iqbal_Academy_Pakistan_7-4"><a href="#cite_note-Iqbal_Academy_Pakistan-7">[7]</a></sup> His birthday <i>Yōm-e Welādat-e Muḥammad Iqbāl</i> (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Urdu_language" title="Urdu language">Urdu</a>: <span dir="rtl" lang="ur" xml:lang="ur"><span class="Nastaliq" style="font-size: 125%; font-family: 'Jameel Noori Nastaleeq', 'Urdu Typesetting', 'Noto Nastaliq Urdu', 'Noto Nastaliq Urdu Draft', 'Hussaini Nastaleeq', 'AlQalam Taj Nastaleeq', IranNastaliq, 'Awami Nastaliq', 'Awami Nastaliq Beta4', 'Awami Nastaliq Beta3', 'Awami Nastaliq Beta2', 'Awami Nastaliq Beta1', 'Nafees Nastaleeq', 'Nafees Nastaleeq v1.01', 'Pak Nastaleeq', 'PDMS_Jauhar', 'Alvi Lahori Nastaleeq';" title="Nastaliq">یوم ولادت محمد اقبال</span></span>‎), or <a href="/wiki/Iqbal_Day" title="Iqbal Day">Iqbal Day</a>, is a <a href="/wiki/Public_holidays_in_Pakistan" title="Public holidays in Pakistan">public holiday in Pakistan</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-brecorder.com_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-brecorder.com-14">[14]</a></sup> In India he is also remembered as the author of the popular song <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Saare_Jahaan_Se_Achcha" title="Saare Jahaan Se Achcha">Saare Jahaan Se Achcha</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup></p>
<p></p>
